## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / constitutive modeling in materials science (thermo-mechanical stress–strain behavior)
**Analysis**: The task maps strain (epsilon) and temperature (T) to stress (sigma), which is the core constitutive-relation problem in solid mechanics/materials science. Common relationships include elastic (Hookean/thermoelastic), elastic–plastic with strain hardening, and temperature-dependent softening of modulus and flow/yield stress.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime, isothermal)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies approximately linearly with temperature over a limited range)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (empirical elastic softening/stiffening with T)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (constrained thermal expansion; c1 acts like thermal expansion coefficient)
- Nonlinear (Landau-type) elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon^3 (finite-strain/nonlinear elastic response at moderate strains)
- Strain hardening power law with temperature prefactor: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * (c2 + Abs(epsilon))^c3 (plastic flow curve with temperature-dependent strength level)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit; common explicit surrogate): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + Abs(epsilon)) + c2 * Abs(epsilon)^c3 (elastic-to-plastic transition with smooth hardening)
- Voce-type saturation hardening with temperature softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * T)) * (c3 - c4 * exp(-c5 * Abs(epsilon))) (approach to saturation stress with strain; overall level varies with T)
- Johnson–Cook-like (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)^c2) * (c3 + c4 * T)^c5 (strain hardening times thermal softening factor)
- Zerilli–Armstrong-like (reduced form without strain-rate): sigma = c0 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)^c2 + c3 * exp(c4 * T) (additive athermal + thermal components)
- Eyring/thermal-activation-like flow stress (reduced): sigma = c0 + c1 * T * asinh(c2 * Abs(epsilon)) (thermally activated plasticity surrogate where stress scales with T and inverse-sinh)
- Elastic–plastic piecewise (yield with T dependence, using smooth switch): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon - (c2 + c3 * T) * tanh(c4 * epsilon) (captures an initial elastic slope and a yield-like reduction in tangent modulus)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon; temperature enters mainly by scaling the proportionality (E(T))
- Thermal expansion under constraint → sigma depends on an effective mechanical strain (epsilon minus a term proportional to T)
- Thermal softening of strength → multiplicative factors decreasing with T (e.g., exp(c*T) with negative c, or (c0 + c1*T)^c2 with negative exponent) reduce sigma at higher T
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → rational or smooth-switch forms in epsilon (e.g., epsilon/(c+|epsilon|), tanh(c*epsilon)) mimic yield onset without explicit piecewise definitions
- Strain hardening → sigma increasing sublinearly/superlinearly with |epsilon| via |epsilon|^n or saturation forms (1 - exp(-c*|epsilon|))
- Saturation/Voce hardening → sigma approaching an asymptote as epsilon grows, often via (c0 - c1*exp(-c2*|epsilon|))
- Nonlinear elasticity at moderate strain → odd polynomial terms (epsilon^3) added to the linear term preserve tension–compression symmetry
- Separable vs nonseparable thermo-mechanical coupling → products like f(T)*g(epsilon) imply uniform thermal scaling of the whole curve, while sums f(epsilon)+g(T) imply independent athermal and thermal components
- Symmetry with respect to sign of strain → using Abs(epsilon) in plastic-flow magnitudes reflects similar response in tension/compression when only magnitude matters

Final search results
============================================================
Best expression     : T*c0 + c1*sin(c2*epsilon + c3) + c4*exp(c5*epsilon) + Abs(T)**c6*Abs(epsilon)**c7
Structure desc      : Purely additive mix of: linear-in-T baseline (T*c0), a sinusoid in epsilon, a decaying exponential in epsilon, and a separable power-law interaction |T|^c6|epsilon|^c7. epsilon appears inside sin and exp and as a magnitude power; T appears linearly and inside the magnitude power (nonlinear scaling). With c0≈-0.216 the linear T term is small, while the dominant variations come from the large-amplitude sine (c1≈32.3), the sizable exponential prefactor (c4≈45.8) with strong decay rate (c5≈-3.76), and a superlinear interaction (|T|^1.25|epsilon|^3.21) that can dominate for large |T| and |epsilon|.
Fitted params       : c0=-2.1635e-01, c1=3.2256e+01, c2=5.0000e+00, c3=1.0042e+00, c4=4.5828e+01, c5=-3.7592e+00, c6=1.2468e+00, c7=3.2052e+00
Train NMSE          : 5.22e-09
Test NMSE           : 6.08e-09
OOD Test NMSE       : 7.83e-07

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci9)
============================================================
GT: c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*(T - c3) + epsilon**c4*c5*(T - c6)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) simplifies to a very specific polynomial-in-ε with an affine dependence on T:
\[
4.2558304788\,\epsilon^3\;-\;0.3902956878\,(T-308.8646781)\;+\;8.6380281543\,\epsilon^3\,(T-308.8646781).
\]
Expand/group by powers of ε and T:
\[
= \underbrace{(8.6380281543)\,\epsilon^3}_{\text{coefficient of }T}\,T \;+\;\underbrace{(4.2558304788-8.6380281543\cdot 308.8646781)}_{\text{constant in }T}\epsilon^3 \;+\;(-0.3902956878)T \;+\;0.3902956878\cdot 308.8646781.
\]
So the GT has exactly these structural features:
- a **cross term** \(T\epsilon^3\) with nonzero coefficient,
- a **pure** \(\epsilon^3\) term,
- a **pure** \(T\) term,
- a **constant** term,
- and **no** \(\epsilon\), \(\epsilon^2\), trig, exp, log, tanh, absolute-power artifacts, etc.

Therefore any candidate must be able (by choosing its free constants) to represent **simultaneously**: \(T\epsilon^3\), \(\epsilon^3\), \(T\), and constant, with all other functional forms removable.

Now check candidates:

1. \(T c0 + c1\sin(\cdot)+c4 e^{c5\epsilon}+|T|^{c6}|\epsilon|^{c7}\).  
   Can create \(T\) via \(Tc0\). Can create \(T\epsilon^3\) only if \(|T|^{c6}|\epsilon|^{c7}\) becomes \(T\epsilon^3\), but that would require \(c6=1,c7=3\) and also \(|T|=T\) (domain \(T\ge0\)). Then you still cannot separately create a **pure** \(\epsilon^3\) term (no such term unless you misuse the same abs-power term, but then you’d lose the \(T\epsilon^3\) cross). So cannot match.

2. Similar to (1) plus linear \(\epsilon\). Still lacks an independent pure \(\epsilon^3\) term and has unwanted \(\epsilon\) unless set to 0. No match.

3. Contains only \(\epsilon\), constants, exponentials in \(\epsilon\), and \(\epsilon e^{T c9}\). No way to get affine-in-\(T\) terms (\(T\) and \(T\epsilon^3\)) without exponentials. No match.

4. Like (3) but \(e^{Tc9}\) without \(\epsilon\). Still not affine in \(T\). No match.

5. \(Tc0 + \sin + e^{c5\epsilon} + c6\epsilon^3 + \epsilon + |T|^{c7}|\epsilon|^{c8}\).  
   You can set sin/exp/ε terms to 0. You can get \(T\) via \(Tc0\), and \(\epsilon^3\) via \(c6\epsilon^3\). For \(T\epsilon^3\), you’d need the abs-power term to be \(T\epsilon^3\) (take \(c7=1,c8=3\) and domain \(T\ge0,\epsilon\ge0\)). But then that abs-power term is exactly \(T\epsilon^3\) and does not introduce extra pieces. This looks promising structurally.  
   However, the abs-power term is \( |T|^{1}|\epsilon|^{3} = T\epsilon^3\) under \(T,\epsilon\ge0\), yes. Then the candidate becomes:
   \[
   Tc0 + c6\epsilon^3 + c_{\text{abs}}\,T\epsilon^3
   \]
   (after zeroing other coefficients). But GT also has a **constant** term (from \(-c2(T-c3)\) expansion gives \(+c2c3\)). Candidate 5 has **no standalone constant** once we zero sin/exp and remove ε. So it cannot match the constant offset. No match.

6. Purely ε-dependent (plus constants), no T. No match.

7. Has \(\epsilon e^{Tc9}\) and \(\epsilon^2\); not affine in T. No match.

8. No plain \(T\) term except via abs-power; but then cannot get both \(T\) and \(T\epsilon^3\) and \(\epsilon^3\) cleanly. Also lacks a clean constant+T structure. No match.

9. \(Tc0 + c1\epsilon + c2 + \sin + c6|T|^{c7}|\epsilon|^{c8} + c9\epsilon\).  
   Has constant \(c2\) and \(Tc0\). Can make \(T\epsilon^3\) via abs-power with \(c7=1,c8=3\) (domain \(T,\epsilon\ge0\)). But then still lacks a pure \(\epsilon^3\) term. No match.

10. \(Tc0 + \sin + e^{c5\epsilon} + c6\epsilon^3 + |T|^{c7}|\epsilon|^{c8}\).  
   Can set sin/exp to 0. Get \(T\) via \(Tc0\), \(\epsilon^3\) via \(c6\epsilon^3\), \(T\epsilon^3\) via abs-power with \(c7=1,c8=3\) and \(T,\epsilon\ge0\). But again: **no standalone constant term**. GT has a nonzero constant \(c2c3\). No match.

11. No affine T; has \(\epsilon e^{Tc9}\). No match.

12. Has \(e^{Tc9}\), not affine. No match.

13–20. These are built from \(T\tanh(\epsilon)\), \(T\epsilon^3\), linear ε, constants, and complicated exp(cos(log(...T...))).  
   You can zero the complicated exp term by setting its prefactor to 0. You can also zero unwanted \(T\tanh(\epsilon)\) by setting its coefficient to 0. Many include \(T\epsilon^3\) which is good. But **none** of 13–20 include an independent pure \(\epsilon^3\) term (without T) *and* an independent pure \(T\) term (without ε) in the same expression in a way that matches GT. They typically have \(T\epsilon^3\) and maybe constants/linear ε, but not the required separate \(T\) term and \(\epsilon^3\) term simultaneously. So no match.

21. Has \(Tc0\) and ε-polynomial pieces but no \(T\epsilon^3\) cross term. No match.

22. \(Tc0 + \sin + e^{c5\epsilon} + c6\epsilon + \epsilon + |T|^{c7}|\epsilon|^{c8}\).  
   No pure \(\epsilon^3\) term. No match.

23–27. Have \(T\epsilon\), \(T\tanh\), \(T\epsilon^3\), etc., plus constants/exp terms. Again, no way to produce simultaneously: pure \(T\) term, pure \(\epsilon^3\) term, and cross \(T\epsilon^3\) term, while removing other T-dependent nonlinearities. No match.

28–35. Include logs, abs-powers, etc. Some can create \(T\) and constants, and abs-power could create \(T\epsilon^3\). But none also provide a clean independent pure \(\epsilon^3\) term (except via an \(\epsilon\cdot|\epsilon|^{c9}\) style in 35, which could make \(\epsilon^3\) by choosing \(c9=2\) and domain \(\epsilon\ge0\)).  
   Check 35 specifically: \(Tc0 + c1\epsilon + c2 + c3\log(Tc4+1) + c5|T|^{c6}|\epsilon|^{c7} + c8\epsilon|\epsilon|^{c9}\).  
   - Set log term off: \(c3=0\).  
   - Set linear ε off: \(c1=0\).  
   - Make cross term \(T\epsilon^3\): choose \(c6=1,c7=3\), domain \(T,\epsilon\ge0\).  
   - Make pure \(\epsilon^3\): choose \(c9=2\) so \(\epsilon|\epsilon|^{2}=\epsilon^3\) (domain \(\epsilon\ge0\)), and set \(c8\) accordingly.  
   - Constant term via \(c2\).  
   This leaves \(Tc0 + c2 + c5 T\epsilon^3 + c8 \epsilon^3\).  
   **But GT also has a pure \(T\) term and a constant term; candidate has pure \(T\) via \(Tc0\) and constant via \(c2\), good.**  
   So structurally candidate 35 *can* represent \(T\), constant, \(T\epsilon^3\), and \(\epsilon^3\) simultaneously. Now check if it can match the exact GT coefficients: yes, because \(c0,c2,c5,c8\) are free and can be set to the needed values. Therefore candidate 35 can match GT on domain \(T\ge0,\epsilon\ge0\).  
   (No remaining extra terms after setting \(c1=c3=0\).)

36. No T. No match.

37. Has \(T\epsilon\) not \(T\) alone; no way to get pure \(T\) term. No match.

38. No \(T\) except abs-power; cannot get both pure \(T\) and cross \(T\epsilon^3\) and pure \(\epsilon^3\) cleanly. No match.

39–44. Lack required cross \(T\epsilon^3\) and/or pure \(T\) and constant simultaneously. No match.

45. Has log(Tc5+1) not affine; cannot match exactly for all T. No match.

46. No pure \(T\) term at all. No match.

47. Has \(Tc0\) and constants and abs-power terms, but no pure \(\epsilon^3\) term. No match.

48–50. Lack pure \(\epsilon^3\) and/or constant and/or cross term. No match.

Conclusion: only candidate **35** can be made identical to GT (under the standard physical-domain relaxation \(T\ge0,\epsilon\ge0\)) by choosing parameters to match the four required coefficients and zeroing the log/linear terms.
